< review>
I love Gomo's Fish Market. Whenever I‚Äôm hungry and in Inglewood CA, I think of  Gomo‚Äôs Fish Market. Gomo‚Äôs is a take-out restaurant that has the best seafood gumbo in Los Angeles. My wife and children love the fried shrimp lunch special. The coating on the shrimp is amazing. My favorite is the charbroiled filet of Sole in garlic butter sauce. It is served to me on a bed of rice and a side of greens. It‚Äôs very delicious. Steven takes my order, give me an estimated time the food will be ready, and hands my prepared food when it‚Äôs ready. I highlight Steve because he‚Äôs so cool. He does not mind giving you ask for extra bread or hot sauce without extra charge. Gomo‚Äôs hot sauce is so good that many people ask for extra. You can also buy fresh fish and have it cooked for you. The prices at Gomo's are reasonable. I highly recommended Gomo‚Äôs Fish Market.<//review>

< Text>
This is my go-to fish market 4 the best in fried catfish fillets. Seasoned to perfection crust is always on point. Really good bang for your buck as they sell by the pound, and they're gumbo is on point as well. The owner is a really nice guy business conscious and the business seems to be blowing up, when I was there last the phone never stopped ringing. Once I even came there with some shrimp and small lobster tails that were going to go bad in my freezer that I thawed out and he breaded and fried them up for me for five bucks.<//Text>

<rating>5</rating><Text>This is the best fish on this side of town. The fish is well seasoned without being salty. I don't usually like filet of sole, however, there is something about their filet of sole.  It is delicious. The french fries are good too.  I get them with no salt. I haven't had much luck with the other sides, but I'm very picky. I think my husband said the greens were good there. My husband loves the catfish and orange roughy. They also have sanddabs and they grill fish too. The tartar sauce is made in house and is very good.  If you like tartar, make sure you get extra.  There is an extra charge though.  Don't be put off because it is a hole in the wall kinda place, as most fish markets are.  The kitchen is very clean and they have an A rating.  I almost forgot the jumbo shrimp....mmmmmm good!< /Text>< gmapID>

<user_id>103309297991948910575<//user_id><user_name>Glen Inokuchi<//user_name>< time>
1598163497303<//time>
<Rate>5</Rate>< text>
This is one of my favorite places to eat in the South Bay.  They have a few  other locations but I have been to this one the most.  I like that its kind of cozy so it isn't too big so large groups over 8 would be tough. Parking lot is a bit small but there is a Post Office parking lot you can use after hours. Their menu is full of normal Mexican fare and there are combinations. They also have a kids menu they hand out with crayons. Personally my go tos are, I love the soup (Xolchi, pronounced sol-chee) It has chicken rice and avocados, it is hearty and healthy especially if you're feeling under the weather.  My other favorite are all the burritos are great, one of my favorites is the Asher (it has egg, chicken & Avocado).  They have great fresh chips and salsa too.  The staff is always amazing and helpful.  My kids loves it too.<//text>

<Rating>2</Rating>< Text>
I kind of hate giving a negative review on a business when the staff are so friendly and helpful, but I went to this restaurant because Google maps recommended it and from the photos on Google maps, I thought the food looked tasty.

If you have ever been to England or heard about the lack of seasoning in their food, you might begin to understand why I was so disappointed with El Gringo Manhattan. Actually, the difference between this place and food in England is that every item the three of us has at El Gringo was so very salty, when in England there isn't much salt or any other seasoning in their food.

The other problem my family and I had was the lack of taste besides salt and a hint of metallic flavor in each item.

So, I had a one item combination meal for $11, a chili relano for $5 and a Shirley Temple that cost a whopping $3.75. That drink taste like a weak Sprite. My 12 soda lover wouldn't drink the entire soda. My wife had an alacart enchilada that cost $4 and my daughter had a barrito with a salad off the kids menu. All of that equaled just over $28.

That was a one timer for all of us.
If you like salty American style Mexican food, then you will probably enjoy El Gringo Manhattan. If you only like the real thing and not seasoned with a truck load of salt like me and my family, then I wouldn't recommend this place.<//Text>

< review>
So disappointing after really looking forward to trying this place.

The setting in the patio is really lovely. So was the special tomato salad.

The food however was really underwhelming. The clam linguine was so salty, it was inedible.  Luckily my partner does not mind super food.

The duck was well cooked but the pappardelle was not. It was either dry or overcooked. The rigatoni was the most successful dish, though also on the salty side but at least still tasty.

The two stars are basically for the tomato salad and the chocolate oblivion cake. Two of of the five dishes that are worth it.

On the upside: dog and stroller friendly.< /review>

< Review>
Had a wonderful dinner at Sociale last week. We ordered the following appetizers (all 5*)- burrata, soup, fig salad, and fried olives. Olives were a little too salty for my liking but others in my party enjoyed them. Main course- artichoke ravioli, pici bolognese, rigatoni, and pappardelle with braised duck. While all of them were delicious, braised duck pasta was the best!
Their beautiful patio coupled with top notch service was a treat. They are also taking required precautions during this pandemic.< /Review>

<review>My husband and I went to Sociale on a Friday night to celebrate our anniversary. We made reservations for 6pm, and we arrived about ten minutes early. We were immediately seated and offered water. We chose a half bottle of red (a very good Brunello) to have with dinner and let our server, Molly, know that one of us was a vegetarian. Molly was terrific throughout the entire meal, even wishing us a happy anniversary (which I had put on the reservation but neither of us had mentioned upon arrival). When I asked her preference between two entr√©es, she didn't hesitate to offer her opinion, which was really nice in contrast to places where you wonder if the people working there have ever sampled the menu. We enjoyed small but very yummy bread rolls while we waited for dinner.

We had a stone fruit and kale salad to start, followed by the wagu beef (for my husband) and the corn tortellini (for me) and polenta fries (to share). Everything was cooked very well and tasted delicious, and the portions were perfect.

For dessert, we enjoyed the orange flan and a vanilla milkshake with a fried dough pastry. Both were just as tasty as everything else we had shared and a perfect end to our meal. Dinner for the two of us, including a shared appetizer, two entrees, a shared side, two desserts, and a half bottle of wine came to about $180, which was very reasonable considering the terrific service and the delicious food. We'll definitely return!<//review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>

< Text>
Sociale is super cute. I love how it's hidden off the street between buildings. The main room and secondary room aesthetic seemed a bit off... a bit funeral home-y with the thick draperies over fake, brick walls and simple, white paint on other walls. Not a ton of charm on the interior, but the patio was adorable.

Service was spectacular - there was quite a long wait between starter and entree (the server didn't even take our dinner order until after the small plates were finished), as other reviewers had mentioned, but that didn't bother me so much. It was a very casual and relaxed environment to enjoy conversation and good food.

We had the fried olives and the pork belly, which were both delicious. They also serve small, warm biscuits/rolls with butter. I love that they were warm and... well... I love bread.

For dinner, I had the Wagyu Bavette Steak. I was a little disappointed - for the price, I really expected something pretty great, but it was a tough cut of meat that was overdone and had a pretty bland and overall game-y flavor.

The wine selection is pretty good and pretty extensive.

I would consider giving it another go and possibly trying the pasta instead, but at this point, I would not recommend to my friends.<//Text>

<text>Based on reviews, I took my kids here. Right when we walked in we were greeted and asked what we were looking for. There were plenty of barber chairs, about 10, and we got right in. This was the day before school started and I was glad to get in so quickly. Two boys got $20 fades w/line-up. Older son got a little longer top style that was also $20. After being there for a minute I noticed the shampoo station and inquired about my daughter also getting her hair done. Miss Cherry was available and willing, she even went to the store and got the EZBraid hair. For cornrows with added hair, a few bangs and two rows at the back of the neck, $80. She added the decorations for free. There were bathrooms and parking available. My boys had to sit while their sister had her hair done, but everyone was very nice and understanding.
Fast forward a few days, my daughter has small red bumps on her scalp and has scratched it raw in a few areas. So I called and was told to bring her in and Miss Cherry would look at it. She put some aloe gel and some anti-itch scalp oil throughout the scalp and suggested to continue doing so. The style lasted three weeks. The Salvation Army used to have a store out back that offered lower prices, but they closed it.  It stands to reason that, in doing so, they lost their less-well-off customers who could no longer afford their higher prices.
